                                       **Files changed**
                                       - `/Users/steve/projects/explore/server/src/logger.ts`
                                       - `/Users/steve/projects/explore/server/src/chat.ts`

                                       **Typing approach**
                                       Every payload logged anywhere in the server — `ClientMessage`,
                                       `ServerEvent`, `ClaudeStreamEvent`, and the ad-hoc lifecycle literals
                                       — carries a `type: string` discriminant, so I added a minimal
                                       structural interface `LoggableEvent { type: string }` in logger.ts
                                       and changed the signature to `log&lt;E extends
                                       LoggableEvent&gt;(source: LogSource, event: E)`. The generic (rather
                                       than a plain `LoggableEvent` parameter) matters because TypeScript's
                                       excess-property check would otherwise reject the ~13 inline literals
                                       like `{ type: "claude:exit", code }`; with inference, each literal's
                                       own type becomes `E` and passes. This let both double casts in
                                       chat.ts (`redactDataUrls(message) as unknown as Record&lt;string,
                                       unknown&gt;` at the old line 183 and `event as unknown as
                                       Record&lt;string, unknown&gt;` in `publish()`) be deleted, with the
                                       union types now flowing through directly. Runtime behavior is
                                       unchanged — the spread in `log` still serializes all fields.

                                       **Verification**
                                       - `npm run typecheck -w server` — passed (after the generic fix; the
                                       non-generic first attempt surfaced the excess-property errors above)
                                       - `npm run lint -w server` (oxlint) — passed
                                       - `npx tsc -p tests --noEmit` — passed (the root typecheck script
                                       also covers this project)</result>

                                       <result>Confirmed the cascade: the plugin's backtick rule sits in
                                       `@layer utilities`, my override is unlayered (and later), so it wins
                                       unconditionally. Done.

                                       ## Root cause

                                       The markdown pipeline was never the problem. I reproduced it
                                       statically by running the exact pipeline (react-markdown + remark-gfm
                                       + the app's rehype-sanitize schema + rehype-slug) through
                                       `renderToStaticMarkup` from `client/node_modules`: `` `inline code`
                                       `` correctly produces `&lt;p&gt;Some &lt;code&gt;inline
                                       code&lt;/code&gt; here…&lt;/p&gt;`, so rehype-sanitize strips
                                       nothing.

                                       The cause was CSS on the `prose` surface (chat messages — the surface
                                       that existed when the bug was noticed 2026-07-07).
                                       `@tailwindcss/typography`'s default inline-code style is:

                                       ```css
                                       .prose :where(code):not(...) { color: ...; font-size: .875em;
                                       font-weight: 600 }
                                       .prose :where(code):not(...)::before, ...::after { content: "`" }
                                       ```

                                       i.e. it re-draws literal backticks as pseudo-elements and gives
                                       inline code no background chip — so `` `foo` `` still displays as ``
                                       `foo` `` and reads as unrendered markdown. (The wiki-document surface
                                       is separately mid-migration by another agent to the new
                                       `client/src/typeset.css`, whose `:not(pre) &gt; code` chip rule
                                       already handles it there; I did not touch that work.)

                                       ## Files changed

                                       - `/Users/steve/projects/explore/client/src/index.css` (only file
                                       touched): appended an unlayered override next to the existing
                                       prose/typeset glue — kills the `::before/::after` backtick content
                                       and gives `.prose :where(:not(pre) &gt; code)` typeset's chip
                                       treatment (`color-mix(in oklab, currentColor 10%, transparent)`
                                       background so `prose-invert` surfaces work, matching radius/padding).
                                       Unlayered on purpose so it beats the plugin's `@layer utilities`
                                       rules; a comment in the file records this.

                                       ## Verification

                                       - Static pipeline render (node, client's own deps): inline backticks
                                       emit `&lt;code&gt;` — pipeline sound.
                                       - `npm run build` in `client/` (which is `tsc -b &amp;&amp; vite
                                       build`, the workspace's typecheck+build): passes. No install run.
                                       - Inspected the built CSS: the override rules are emitted
                                       (`content:none` + chip), positioned after and outside the plugin's
                                       `@layer utilities` backtick rule — confirmed programmatically that
                                       the plugin rule is layered and mine is not, so the override wins by
                                       cascade rules regardless of order. Selector specificity is identical
                                       (`:where()` on both), so there's no fragility there.

                                       Note for the caller: `client/src/components/markdown.tsx`,
                                       `file-viewer.tsx`, and `index.css` carry concurrent uncommitted edits
                                       from another agent (typeset migration, `oui-embed`); my change is a
                                       pure append to `index.css` and doesn't conflict.</result>

                                       # Cuelume: Interaction Sounds for the Web
                                       ## What It Is
                                       Cuelume is a lightweight library that generates interaction sounds
                                       using Web Audio synthesis. It creates audio cues that respond to user
                                       interactions, making interfaces feel more responsive and engaging.
                                       ## What It Does
                                       The tool synthesizes 10 different sound cues (chime, sparkle,
                                       droplet, bloom, whisper, tick, press, release, toggle, success) in
                                       real-time. You can trigger sounds through HTML attributes tied to
                                       user interactions like hovering, pressing, releasing, or toggling
                                       elements, or call the sound playback function programmatically.
                                       last lines:
                                       3. Call `bind()` to activate attribute-based sounds, or use `play()`
                                       for manual triggers
                                       ## "Realtime Feedback" Context
                                       In this project, realtime feedback refers to the immediate auditory
                                       response generated when users interact with interface elements—"Tiny
                                       interaction sounds that make interfaces feel alive." The sounds are
                                       synthesized instantly during interaction rather than loading
                                       pre-recorded files.

2026-07-12 06:02:35  ASSISTANT:        Cuelume is installed and wired up. Summary of what it is and what I
                                       did:

                                       **What Cuelume is:** a tiny MIT-licensed npm library
                                       (`cuelume@0.1.0`) that synthesizes interaction sounds live via the
                                       Web Audio API — ten cues like `press`, `release`, `toggle`, `success`
                                       — triggered declaratively through `data-cuelume-*` attributes. No
                                       audio files, zero dependencies. Since it was published just yesterday
                                       by a single maintainer, I inspected the full tarball before
                                       installing: 330 lines of plain Web Audio synthesis, no network calls,
                                       no eval, nothing suspicious.

                                       **Wiring (kept minimal and away from files other agents are
                                       editing):**
                                       - `client/src/main.tsx` — one `bind()` call at startup; it uses
                                       delegated listeners, so every current and future `data-cuelume-*`
                                       element in the app is covered.
                                       - Toolbar (`main-toolbar.tsx`) — press cue on Home, toggle cues on
                                       the drawing-mode and chat-panel toggles, and a `success` cue on the
                                       artifact Save button.
                                       - Chat sidebar (`chat-sidebar.tsx`) — press/release on Send, press on
                                       the screenshot button, toggle on close.

                                       Sounds are mouse-driven per the library (press/release are
                                       mouse-only; hover cues I skipped as too chatty for this UI). If you
                                       want a sound-off preference later, the library exposes
                                       `setEnabled(false)` for the app to own the setting.

                                       **Verification:** the client bundles cleanly with the new import and
                                       lint is clean on my files. A full typecheck is currently impossible
                                       through no fault of this change — the voice-agent work has
                                       `use-chat.ts` mid-edit and red. Both pending commits (the cuelume
                                       change, plus the earlier TASKS.md/worklog blitz bookkeeping) are
                                       queued behind the repo's typecheck+lint commit gate; I have a
                                       background watcher that will land them as soon as the tree goes
                                       green. The commit will also carry the other agent's one-line
                                       `rehype-raw` dependency entry in `package.json`/lockfile —
                                       unavoidable since `npm install` regenerates the lockfile from the
                                       shared working tree, and keeping those two files consistent beats
                                       splitting them.

2026-07-12 06:08:19  ASSISTANT:        Reworked per your direction — I caught and stopped the pending commit
                                       before the button-sound version landed, so none of that shipped.

                                       **What changed:**
                                       - **All per-click sounds removed.** Every `data-cuelume-*` attribute
                                       I'd added (toolbar, send, screenshot, close, and the mic button) is
                                       gone, along with the `bind()` call — cuelume is now used imperatively
                                       only.
                                       - **Server-pushed events:** new `client/src/lib/sound-cues.ts` with
                                       `useServerEventSounds` — plays a soft chime when a `wiki:changed`
                                       event from the server matches the document currently on screen, i.e.
                                       the LLM or voice agent just edited what you're reading. It's keyed to
                                       the same `app/wiki-changed` store signal the file viewer uses for
                                       hot-reload, and seeded with the mount-time sequence number so nothing
                                       chimes on load. Easy to extend with more server events later.
                                       - **Voice on/off:** `useVoiceSounds` watches the voice session status
                                       from the new `use-voice` hook — a warm "bloom" when the session
                                       actually becomes live (listening, not merely connecting), and a
                                       falling "droplet" when it ends, including error teardown, so an open
                                       mic is always audible. I deliberately keyed it to live-session
                                       transitions rather than the mic button click: listening↔speaking↔tool
                                       flips during conversation stay silent, and you only hear on/off when
                                       the mic truly opens or closes.

                                       Both hooks are called from `App.tsx`, which already has the view and
                                       voice state. Client typecheck and build are green.

                                       **Landing:** my App.tsx wiring sits on top of the voice agent's
                                       uncommitted `use-voice.ts`, so committing now would leave HEAD
                                       referencing a file that isn't in the tree. A background watcher will
                                       commit `sound-cues.ts` + the App.tsx wiring the moment the voice work
                                       is committed and the repo gate is green. (Also noting: the cuelume
                                       dependency entry and my earlier blitz bookkeeping already reached
                                       HEAD — other agents' commits swept those files in, which on this
                                       shared checkout is fine.)

                                       - **Server-pushed edit chime** — `useServerEventSounds` chimes when a
                                       `wiki:changed` event matches the document currently on screen, and
                                       stays silent otherwise (including on page load, via the mount-time
                                       sequence guard).
                                       - **Voice on/off cues** — `useVoiceSounds` plays a warm bloom when
                                       the mic session actually goes live and a falling droplet when it ends
                                       (including error teardown). Mid-conversation listening↔speaking↔tool
                                       transitions are silent by design.
                                       - The commit also carries the voice agent's three App.tsx wiring
                                       lines (`useVoice` + the `voice` prop) — their `use-voice.ts` hook was
                                       already committed, my hook call depends on that wiring, and it's the
                                       same file on the shared checkout; the commit message records this.

                                       One process note from this session worth remembering: `git commit --
                                       <path>` silently can't commit *new* files (pathspec error), which is
                                       what tripped the background watcher — the fix was a plain `git add`
                                       first. The `sound-cues.ts` module is the place to add future
                                       server-event cues (e.g., a cue when a delegated voice task completes)
                                       — one `play()` call per event type.

                                       <result>Done. Report:

                                       **Files changed**
                                       - `/Users/steve/projects/explore/client/src/lib/openui.tsx` — Gallery
                                       grid (~line 241) and Aside grid (~line 318) column templates, plus
                                       the `navWidth`/`asideWidth` schema descriptions.
                                       - `/Users/steve/projects/explore/server/src/ui-library.ts` — same two
                                       description updates (file header mandates it stay in sync with the
                                       client schemas; it's what generates the LLM system prompt).

                                       **Mechanism chosen: cap the fixed column with `min()`, no container
                                       queries**
                                       - Gallery: `gridTemplateColumns: min(${navWidth ?? "240px"}, 40%)
                                       minmax(0, 1fr)`
                                       - Aside: `gridTemplateColumns: minmax(0, 1fr) min(${asideWidth ??
                                       "280px"}, 40%)`

                                       Why this over the alternatives in the brief:
                                       - `fit-content(Xpx)` / `minmax(auto, Xpx)` don't help: under the grid
                                       track-sizing algorithm the intrinsic track still grows toward X
                                       before the `1fr` track (whose min is 0) gets anything, so the
                                       flexible column is still the one that crushes. Only tying the fixed
                                       column to the container size fixes the priority.
                                       - A container query stacking the columns can't be done as suggested:
                                       a `@container` rule cannot style the container element itself, so
                                       `container-type` on the wrapper wouldn't let us change the wrapper's
                                       own `grid-template-columns`. Doing it properly would require either
                                       an extra DOM wrapper (breaking artifact CSS that targets
                                       `.gallery`/`.aside-layout` as the grid) or sprinkling
                                       `container-type` + `!important` overrides across several hook-class
                                       elements. The `min()` cap is one expression per component, keeps
                                       inline styles (artifact CSS can still override), adds no DOM, and
                                       works at any nesting depth because the 40% resolves against the
                                       immediate grid container (a Gallery inside `aside-main` scales to
                                       that column, not the viewport).

                                       **Behavior at the three widths**
                                       - Full panel and 72rem embed breakout: 40% ≥ 461px/288px, both
                                       defaults (240/280px) and wild-artifact values like 300px are below
                                       the cap — pixel-identical to before.
                                       - 48rem (768px container): cap is 307px; 240/280/300px all still
                                       render at their requested width — the current embed breakout remains
                                       a pure win for wide artifacts but is no longer load-bearing for
                                       defaults.
                                       - Narrow (e.g. 400px): nav/aside shrink to 160px, main/detail keeps
                                       240px — the flexible column is now guaranteed ≥ 60% of the container
                                       at every width instead of absorbing the entire deficit (previously
                                       400 − 280 = 120px one-word lines). Explicit pixel props from existing
                                       artifacts remain accepted; they're now a maximum.

                                       **D4 compliance:** no chrome added, hook classes and DOM unchanged,
                                       inline style still overridable by artifact stylesheets; schema
                                       descriptions updated so the LLM knows widths are maxima with a 60%
                                       floor for the main column.

                                       **Verification:** `npm run typecheck -w client` clean; `npm run lint
                                       -w client` shows only pre-existing fast-refresh warnings; server
                                       typecheck clean too. There is no client test runner or renderable
                                       fixture harness in the repo (no `*.test.*` files; client scripts are
                                       dev/build/lint/preview/typecheck only), and the eval directory has an
                                       unattended sweep running, so I verified by the CSS reasoning above

                                       **Files changed (mine only):**
                                       - `/Users/steve/projects/explore/client/src/components/markdown.tsx`
                                       — replaced `prose prose-sm max-w-none` / `prose-invert` with `typeset
                                       break-words` + `typeset-docs` (when `typeset` prop) or `typeset-chat`
                                       (default), and `invert` → `typeset-invert`. Updated the stale
                                       prose-referencing comments and prop docs. This also moves the
                                       home-view README excerpt (the other non-typeset caller) onto
                                       `typeset-chat` — nothing in the app renders prose anymore.
                                       - `/Users/steve/projects/explore/client/src/index.css` — added
                                       `.typeset-chat` next to `.typeset-docs` (`--typeset-size: 0.875rem`
                                       matching prose-sm, `--typeset-leading: 1.6`, `--typeset-flow:
                                       0.75em`, explicit `font-size` since base `.typeset` scales 1.125x
                                       below the 48rem *viewport* breakpoint, meaningless in a sidebar;
                                       typeset sets no max-width anywhere, so no `max-width: none` override
                                       was needed) and `.typeset-invert`. Deleted the unlayered `.prose
                                       :where(:not(pre) &gt; code)` backtick-chip override and removed
                                       `.prose` from the select-text rule (now `.typeset, pre, code, input,
                                       textarea`).
                                       -
                                       `/Users/steve/projects/explore/client/src/components/file-viewer.tsx`
                                       — comment-only fix ("compact prose" → "compact typeset-chat").

                                       **Invert / user-bubble contrast:** typeset colors via theme tokens
                                       with currentColor fallbacks (`color: var(--color-foreground,
                                       currentColor)`), and the tokens are always defined, so on the
                                       `bg-primary text-primary-foreground` bubble the theme foreground
                                       would have clobbered the white text. `.typeset-invert` redefines the
                                       tokens locally as currentColor mixes (`--color-foreground:
                                       currentColor`, muted-foreground 75%, muted 10%, border 30%, ring
                                       currentColor), so headings, muted text, rules, chips, and focus rings
                                       all derive from the bubble's own text color. Verified computed styles
                                       in the browser: body/heading `oklch(1 0 0)` (white), del 75% white,
                                       chip 12%→10% white mix.

                                       `--color-muted` as background, which is exactly the assistant

2026-07-12 06:26:27  ASSISTANT:        All three fixes are committed through the gate, plus bookkeeping:

                                       **Container-responsive Gallery/Aside** (`b86362d`) — the fixed
                                       nav/aside column is now `min(<requested width>, 40%)` of the
                                       container, so the main/detail column keeps at least 60% at any width
                                       instead of collapsing to one-word lines. Existing artifacts' explicit
                                       pixel widths still work and render identically at full width — they
                                       just become maxima. The agent ruled out the backlog's suggested
                                       alternatives with good reasons: `fit-content()`/`minmax(auto, X)`
                                       don't help because intrinsic tracks outrank a `1fr` track with min 0
                                       in grid sizing, and a container query can't restyle its own container
                                       element without extra DOM that would break artifact CSS targeting the
                                       hook classes. The LLM-facing component descriptions were updated in
                                       both the client schema and the server's prompt copy.

                                       **Chat on typeset** (`afa8aae`) — chat (and the home README excerpt)
                                       moved to `typeset typeset-chat`, a compact preset matching prose-sm's
                                       size; nothing in the app renders `.prose` anymore, so my earlier
                                       backtick-chip override came out. Inverted user bubbles get
                                       `typeset-invert`, which redefines typeset's color tokens as
                                       currentColor mixes so headings/rules/chips derive from the bubble's
                                       white text. The agent's visual check on the dev server caught a real
                                       bug along the way: typeset's inline-code chip background is
                                       `--color-muted`, exactly the assistant bubble's background, making
                                       chips invisible — fixed with a chat-local token override.

                                       **TypeScript ~6.0.2 everywhere** (`401485f`) — root and server bumped
                                       from `^5.9.3`/`^5.8.0`; all three workspaces now share one hoisted
                                       6.0.3 compiler and client's nested copy deduped away. Zero fallout:
                                       full typecheck+lint green and 65/65 tests pass.

                                       Three new nits went into the blitz backlog instead of being fixed on
                                       sight: refreshing the eval prompt snapshots that mirror the width
                                       descriptions (left alone because the Optimizer's sweep is running
                                       against `eval/`), softening the now-stale "built for the full panel"
                                       comment in oui-embed, and dropping the dead `@tailwindcss/typography`
                                       plugin remnants.

                                       - **New:
                                       `/Users/steve/projects/explore/client/src/lib/view-history.ts`** —
                                       self-contained module: `normalizeView` (moved here from App.tsx so
                                       both App and history share one normalizer), `viewToHash`/`hashToView`
                                       codecs, and a `useViewHistory()` hook (mount-once effect,
                                       takes/returns nothing, mirroring `sound-cues.ts`). No router library.
                                       - **Modified: `/Users/steve/projects/explore/client/src/App.tsx`** —
                                       removed the local `normalizeView`, imports it plus `useViewHistory`
                                       from the new module, and calls `useViewHistory()` once. Did not touch
                                       `chat-sidebar.tsx` / `use-voice.ts`; nothing committed, no installs.

                                       ## URL scheme (hash — no server routing changes; app is Vite
                                       dev-proxy / static dist with no SPA catch-all)
                                       - `#/home`, `#/authoring`, `#/doc` (empty in-memory OUI doc),
                                       `#/doc/&lt;url&gt;` with each segment percent-encoded — e.g.
                                       `#/doc//docs/decisions.md` (double slash because wiki urls start with
                                       `/`; round-trips losslessly).

                                       ## Loop-guard design
                                       - Single integration point: a `subscribeState("app/view", ...)`
                                       listener — every navigation source (toolbar, wiki links, artifact
                                       links, LLM/server `set_state`) flows through that key, so all of them
                                       get history entries.
                                       - `applyingHistory` flag brackets the store write made during
                                       `popstate` (store emits synchronously), so history-driven writes
                                       never push.
                                       - `trackedJson` (JSON of the normalized view) dedupes: store writes
                                       that don't change the view don't push. Verified: clicking Home twice
                                       = exactly one history entry.
                                       - `drawMode`/`chatOpen` live under other store keys and never enter
                                       history.

                                       ## Edge cases handled
                                       - **Initial load**: a view-naming hash seeds the store (deep
                                       link/reload wins over default), then `replaceState` records the first
                                       entry; no hash → `replaceState` of the current/default view.
                                       - **LLM/server-driven changes**: `applyServerUpdates` → `setState` →
                                       same listener, so they push entries and update the URL like clicks.
                                       - **Authoring**: history-tracked like other views (back from
                                       authoring returns to the previous doc); forward into authoring
                                       re-renders whatever `chat.ui.program` currently holds, which is the
                                       existing semantic of that view.
                                       - **Manual hash edits / entries without state**: `popstate` falls
                                       back to parsing `location.hash` when `event.state.view` is absent;
                                       unknown hashes fall back to home.
                                       - **Malformed LLM writes**: all history paths go through
                                       `normalizeView` (bare string → doc view, junk → home).

                                       ## Verification
                                       - `npm run typecheck -w client` clean; `npm run lint -w client` clean
                                       for changed files (only pre-existing fast-refresh warnings
                                       elsewhere); `vite build` to scratchpad succeeded.
                                       - Live browser test against the already-running dev server
                                       (localhost:5173), using a `window` marker to prove no unload: home →
                                       doc link → home button → back → back → forward all moved between
                                       views with the marker intact (SPA never unloaded); manual hash
                                       navigation to another doc worked; hard reload on
                                       `#/doc//docs/decisions.md` deep-linked straight to the doc; no
                                       console errors.

                                       Residual risk: minimal — server-side `set_state` while the user sits
                                       mid-history-stack truncates the forward stack (standard `pushState`
                                       behavior, arguably correct); and a future "authoring" entry restores
                                       whatever program is currently loaded rather than a snapshot, which
                                       matches how the view already worked.</result>

                                       ## Seam driven and why it's faithful
                                       The tests spawn the **real** `server/src/ui-mcp.ts` as a stdio MCP
                                       server using the exact production contract from
                                       `ClaudeSession.writeMcpConfig` (`server/src/claude.ts:357-372`):
                                       `node_modules/.bin/tsx server/src/ui-mcp.ts` with `PORT` in env. They
                                       drive it with the `@modelcontextprotocol/sdk` stdio client (playing
                                       the Claude CLI's role) against a real app server started on an
                                       ephemeral port via the existing `tests/helpers/app.ts` harness, with
                                       `AppSocket` websocket clients playing the browser's role (answering
                                       forwarded `state:update`/`state:request` with `state:response`). So
                                       every production hop is exercised byte-identically — MCP tool →
                                       `serverExchange` ws dial-back (`ui-mcp.ts:193-231`) →
                                       `ChatService.forwardToFrontEnd` relay (`server/src/chat.ts`) →
                                       browser → reply routing back to the tool — with no LLM and no
                                       in-process reconstruction. The bad-port suite reproduces the
                                       historical failure precisely: `startUiMcp("0")`, the literal value
                                       ui-mcp used to inherit when the app bound PORT=0.

                                       ## Regressions caught
                                       1. **PORT=0 silent failure (the banked regression):** with `PORT=0`,
                                       `set_state` and `edit_artifact` must return `isError` results whose
                                       text names the failure (`state update failed:` / `edit failed:`), the
                                       app server must see nothing (`expectSilence` on the browser socket),
                                       and the wiki file must be byte-identical. A return to silent success,
                                       a hang, or a mis-dialed write fails the test.
                                       2. **Correct-port round-trip:** `set_state` updates must reach a
                                       connected browser client verbatim and the applied store must flow
                                       back into the tool reply; `state` must round-trip the browser
                                       snapshot; `edit_artifact` must merge into the `.oui` on disk and
                                       broadcast `wiki:changed` to viewers. Breakage anywhere in
                                       MCP→server→browser routing (id correlation, requester exclusion,
                                       reply forwarding) fails these.
                                       3. **No-browser loud failure:** with only the MCP dial-back
                                       connection present, `set_state` must surface "no front-end client is
                                       connected" as an error — guarding the other silent-failure mode in
                                       the same chain.

                                       ## Vault search probe — findings

                                       ### How the vault is configured
                                       `server/src/claude.ts` (`writeMcpConfig`, lines 354–391) writes an
                                       `mcp.json` per session containing a `vault` server: command
                                       `node_modules/.bin/markdown-vault-mcp`
                                       (`@wirux/mcp-markdown-vault@2.3.0`), env `VAULT_PATH=&lt;wikiDir&gt;`
                                       — which is `docs/` unless `WIKI_DIR` overrides
                                       (`server/src/index.ts:35`). Stdio transport, local embeddings (no
                                       Ollama/Qdrant env set). The CLI is launched with `--disallowedTools
                                       mcp__vault__workflow` (claude.ts:250) — the workflow tool is excluded
                                       from the model's context, everything else is visible.

                                       **Key naming fact:** `search`, `global_search`, `semantic_search` are
                                       not tool names — they are **actions of one `view` tool** (`{action,
                                       query, path?, directory?, maxChunks?}`). The server exposes 5 tools:
                                       `vault`, `edit`, `view`, `workflow`, `system`. So in a CLI session
                                       they'd be called as `mcp__vault__view` with an action argument.

                                       ### Probe results (temp copy of decisions.md, ARCHITECTURE.md,
                                       journeys.md; real state dir untouched)
                                       - `view.search` (path-scoped, query "gpt-realtime"): 52ms — returned
                                       the exact D5 heading-chunked section from decisions.md with
                                       headingPath. Sane.
                                       - `view.global_search` ("ephemeral session tokens"): 655ms — correct
                                       file + section, cross-vault. Sane.
                                       - `view.semantic_search` (paraphrase "how does voice audio reach the
                                       AI model", no literal overlap with target phrasing): 53ms — top hit
                                       was the D5 section. Vector index built automatically at startup (19
                                       chunks from 5 files); `system.status` confirmed `indexingState:
                                       "watching"`, 0 failures. Sane.

                                       ### Semantic index cost
                                       - The embedding model (Xenova/all-MiniLM-L6-v2, **86MB model.onnx**)
                                       was already cached at
                                       `node_modules/@huggingface/transformers/.cache/` — so I observed
                                       warm-start only: full index build for a small vault completes within
                                       server startup (~1–2s). The one-time cost is the 86MB download on
                                       first ever use, and **that cache lives inside node_modules, so a
                                       fresh `npm install`/CI checkout re-downloads it**.
                                       - The real `docs/.markdown_vault_mcp/` index already exists
                                       (index.json 186KB + vectors.bin 250KB, savedAt 2026-07-12T06:41Z) —
                                       semantic search over the real wiki is already warm; a session would
                                       not pay any build cost today.

                                       ### Quirks found
                                       1. **The server mutates the vault on startup**: it auto-creates
                                       `meta/contract.md` and `meta/overview.md` inside `VAULT_PATH` (with a
                                       warning "auto-created in non-empty vault"). This already happened to
                                       the real wiki — `docs/meta/` exists. It's gitignored
                                       (`.gitignore:11`), but it means the vault MCP is not read-only even
                                       before any tool call.
                                       2. The auto-created meta files get indexed too (backlink index
                                       counted 5 files for my 3-file vault) — harmless noise in results.
                                       3. `global_search` is ~10x slower than the other two (still
                                       sub-second on a small vault).

                                       ### What I left in the repo
                                       - `/Users/steve/projects/explore/scripts/probe-vault-mcp.mts` —
                                       manual probe (spawns the vault server over stdio against a temp copy,
                                       exercises list-tools + all three search actions + system.status).
                                       Header comment explains how to run it (`node_modules/.bin/tsx
                                       scripts/probe-vault-mcp.mts`) and why it is **not** an `npm test`
                                       test: on a fresh checkout the startup auto-indexer downloads the 86MB
                                       embedding model — not hermetic, not fast. (`.mts` because the repo
                                       root isn't ESM; scripts/ is outside all tsconfigs, and `npm run
                                       check` exits 0.)
                                       - No commits, no changes to docs/ or the real state dir.

                                       ### Recommendation
                                       Vault search **works and is demo-ready**: all three modes return
                                       correct, well-structured (heading-chunked, path-attributed) results
                                       over real wiki content, and the semantic index for docs/ is already
                                       built. The voice agent's grep-based `wiki-service.ts` search is still
                                       the right call for its path — it's in-process (no MCP round-trip from
                                       the voice tool bridge), hermetic in tests, and covers non-markdown
                                       files the vault can't see — but "the vault is untested" is no longer
                                       a valid part of that rationale. For the Claude CLI session itself,
                                       vault `view` search can be trusted as-is; the only watch-items are
                                       the node_modules-resident model cache (re-download after reinstall)
                                       and the startup write of `docs/meta/*`.</result>

                                       ## D6 feedback envelope — implemented and verified

                                       ### Files changed
                                       - `/Users/steve/projects/explore/server/src/protocol.ts`
                                       - `/Users/steve/projects/explore/client/src/lib/chat-protocol.ts`
                                       (hand-mirrored, as the existing convention: the client file is a

                                       Not committed, no `npm install`, per constraints.

                                       ### The envelope as landed (both protocol files)
                                       ```ts
                                       export interface FeedbackEnvelope {
                                         text?: string;
                                         screenshot?: string;        // base64 data URL
                                         statementRef?: string;      // D4 statement name; no producer yet
                                       (P1)
                                         stateSnapshot?: Record&lt;string, unknown&gt;;  // D3 store at
                                       capture time
                                       }
                                       ```
                                       `ChatCommand extends FeedbackEnvelope` (plus `id` and a legacy
                                       `image` alias); `VoiceTranscriptCommand extends FeedbackEnvelope`
                                       (narrows `text` to required, adds `role`). `ChatMessageEvent` now
                                       echoes `statementRef` and `stateSnapshot` alongside the existing
                                       `image` so every client can render the adornments.

                                       ### Producers / consumers
                                       - **Typed chat + screenshot round-trip** (`use-chat.ts send`): now
                                       emits `{type:"chat", id, text, screenshot, stateSnapshot:
                                       stateSnapshot()}` — the snapshot is always attached, matching the
                                       voice path's convention. `App.tsx screenshot()` needed no change
                                       beyond its comment.
                                       - **Voice transcript**: unchanged on the client (already
                                       envelope-shaped); the server now forwards its `stateSnapshot` on the
                                       `via:"voice"` chat:message broadcast so rows can render the state
                                       chip (the explicitly deferred piece).
                                       - **Server LLM turn** (`chat.ts`): new exported
                                       `withEnvelopeContext(text, envelope)` is the single formatting point
                                       — it prefixes a fenced `&lt;feedback-context&gt;` block carrying
                                       `regarding statement: …` and `state store at capture: {…}` (compact
                                       JSON), passing bare turns through unchanged. Note: voice:transcript
                                       never reaches the Claude session (it's transcript/log only), so there
                                       was no second turn-builder to merge — the helper is where any future
                                       channel plugs in. `redactDataUrls` now also redacts
                                       `chat.screenshot`.
                                       - **Rendering** (`chat-sidebar.tsx`): new `EnvelopeChips` (existing
                                       `Badge` outline variant + lucide icons, no new deps) under the bubble
                                       — a "re: &lt;statement&gt;" chip when `statementRef` is present, and
                                       a compact state chip (filename/mode derived from `app/view`, full
                                       snapshot in the hover tooltip) on user rows and voice assistant rows.
                                       `statementRef` rendering is live even though nothing produces it yet.

                                       ### Compatibility
                                       Server accepts old-shape `{text, image}` chat commands (`screenshot
                                       ?? image`), and `stateSnapshot`/`statementRef` are optional
                                       everywhere — old clients and the pre-change bridge test message shape
                                       still work. Event direction keeps the existing `image` field name.
                                       All producers in this repo now emit the envelope.

                                       ### Verified
                                       - `npm run check` exit 0 (only pre-existing fast-refresh lint
                                       warnings); `npm test`: **71/71 pass** (includes the real-server voice

2026-07-12 06:57:18  USER:             # Claude in Chrome browser automation

                                       You have access to browser automation tools
                                       (mcp__claude-in-chrome__*) for interacting with web pages in Chrome.
                                       Follow these guidelines for effective browser automation.

                                       ## Loading deferred tools

                                       If the mcp__claude-in-chrome__* tools are deferred (must be loaded
                                       via ToolSearch before use), load every tool you expect to need in ONE
                                       ToolSearch call — the select query accepts a comma-separated list —
                                       never one call per tool. Start with the core set:

                                       ToolSearch with query "select:mcp__claude-in-chrome__tabs_context_mcp
                                       ,mcp__claude-in-chrome__navigate,mcp__claude-in-chrome__computer,mcp_
                                       _claude-in-chrome__read_page,mcp__claude-in-chrome__tabs_create_mcp"

                                       Add task-specific tools to the same call when the task obviously
                                       needs them: read_console_messages / read_network_requests for
                                       debugging, form_input for forms, gif_creator for recordings,
                                       javascript_tool for page scripting.

                                       ## GIF recording

                                       When performing multi-step browser interactions that the user may
                                       want to review or share, use mcp__claude-in-chrome__gif_creator to
                                       record them.

                                       You must ALWAYS:
                                       * Capture extra frames before and after taking actions to ensure
                                       smooth playback
                                       * Name the file meaningfully to help the user identify it later
                                       (e.g., "login_process.gif")

                                       ## Console log debugging

                                       You can use mcp__claude-in-chrome__read_console_messages to read
                                       console output. Console output may be verbose. If you are looking for
                                       specific log entries, use the 'pattern' parameter with a
                                       regex-compatible pattern. This filters results efficiently and avoids
                                       overwhelming output. For example, use pattern: "[MyApp]" to filter
                                       for application-specific logs rather than reading all console output.

                                       ## Alerts and dialogs

                                       IMPORTANT: Do not trigger JavaScript alerts, confirms, prompts, or
                                       browser modal dialogs through your actions. These browser dialogs
                                       block all further browser events and will prevent the extension from
                                       receiving any subsequent commands. Instead, when possible, use
                                       console.log for debugging and then use the
                                       mcp__claude-in-chrome__read_console_messages tool to read those log
                                       messages. If a page has dialog-triggering elements:
                                       1. Avoid clicking buttons or links that may trigger alerts (e.g.,
                                       "Delete" buttons with confirmation dialogs)
                                       2. If you must interact with such elements, warn the user first that
                                       this may interrupt the session
                                       3. Use mcp__claude-in-chrome__javascript_tool to check for and
                                       dismiss any existing dialogs before proceeding

                                       If you accidentally trigger a dialog and lose responsiveness, inform
                                       the user they need to manually dismiss it in the browser.

                                       ## Avoid rabbit holes and loops

                                       When using browser automation tools, stay focused on the specific
                                       task. If you encounter any of the following, stop and ask the user
                                       for guidance:
                                       - Unexpected complexity or tangential browser exploration
                                       - Browser tool calls failing or returning errors after 2-3 attempts
                                       - No response from the browser extension
                                       - Page elements not responding to clicks or input
                                       - Pages not loading or timing out
                                       - Unable to complete the browser task despite multiple approaches

                                       Explain what you attempted, what went wrong, and ask how the user
                                       would like to proceed. Do not keep retrying the same failing browser
                                       action or explore unrelated pages without checking in first.

                                       ## Tab context and session startup

                                       IMPORTANT: At the start of each browser automation session, call
                                       mcp__claude-in-chrome__tabs_context_mcp first to get information
                                       about the user's current browser tabs. Use this context to understand
                                       what the user might want to work with before creating new tabs.

                                       Never reuse tab IDs from a previous/other session. Follow these
                                       guidelines:
                                       1. Only reuse an existing tab if the user explicitly asks to work
                                       with it
                                       2. Otherwise, create a new tab with
                                       mcp__claude-in-chrome__tabs_create_mcp
                                       3. If a tool returns an error indicating the tab doesn't exist or is
                                       invalid, call tabs_context_mcp to get fresh tab IDs
                                       4. When a tab is closed by the user or a navigation error occurs,
                                       call tabs_context_mcp to see what tabs are available

2026-07-13 04:25:39  USER:             <task-notification>
                                       <task-id>a314a41d0178a9a7d</task-id>
                                       <tool-use-id>toolu_011Ka4iHYziALEvafnbYSfoe</tool-use-id>
                                       <output-file>/private/tmp/claude-501/-Users-steve-projects-explore/c0
                                       4b8e73-74f7-4e47-8c4e-7d824d2b53d1/tasks/a314a41d0178a9a7d.output</ou

                                       <status>completed</status>
                                       <summary>Agent "Chat pane bottom anchoring" finished</summary>
                                       <note>A task-notification fires each time this agent stops with no
                                       live background children of its own. The user can send it another
                                       message and resume it, so the same task-id may notify more than
                                       once.</note>
                                       <result>Done. Summary:

                                       ## Root cause

                                       The scroller primitive (`@shadcn/react/message-scroller`, used by `/U
                                       sers/steve/projects/explore/client/src/components/ui/message-scroller
                                       .tsx`) already reacts to everything needed: a MutationObserver
                                       (childList) for new items and a ResizeObserver on the Content for
                                       streaming growth — both funnel into "scroll to end, but only while an
                                       internal mode ref is `following-bottom`". Verified live: while
                                       pinned, streaming growth **does** follow.

                                       The bug is the mode machine's escape hatch. The Viewport treats
                                       **every** `wheel`/`touchmove` as scroll-away intent and flips to
                                       `free-scrolling`; the only way back to `following-bottom` is an
                                       actual scroll event landing within 8px of the bottom. A downward (or
                                       horizontal, deltaY=0) wheel tick while already at the bottom moves
                                       nothing, so no scroll event ever fires and the pin is silently,
                                       permanently lost. On macOS trackpads this happens constantly —
                                       inertia keeps emitting wheel events after you reach the bottom, so
                                       even "scroll down to the newest message" unpins itself an instant
                                       after re-pinning. Proved in the live app: pinned + streaming
                                       followed; one synthetic `wheel deltaY:+4` at the bottom → every
                                       subsequent chunk left the view frozen while max-scroll grew.

                                       ## Fix

                                       Wrapper-level, in `client/src/components/ui/message-scroller.tsx`
                                       only (+32 lines; chat-sidebar.tsx untouched, no new observers). The
                                       primitive runs its intent handler before the `onWheel` prop, so
                                       `MessageScrollerViewport` now passes an `onWheel` that immediately
                                       re-pins via the component's own public API
                                       (`useMessageScroller().scrollToEnd`, which restores follow mode) when
                                       the gesture points at the bottom:
                                       - `deltaY &gt; 0` within 100px of the bottom → re-pin (covers inertia
                                       ticks and "wheel back down to the newest message")
                                       - `deltaY === 0` at the bottom (≤2px) → restore the pin in place
                                       (horizontal trackpad pans no longer unpin)
                                       - `deltaY &lt; 0` (scrolling up to read) → untouched, stays unpinned

                                       ## Verification

                                       - `npm run typecheck -w client` passes; client lint: 0 errors (only
                                       pre-existing fast-refresh warnings); vite build to scratchpad
                                       succeeds.
                                       - Live on :5173 via Chrome, simulating streaming by growing a
                                       message's text in the DOM (no childList change — exercises exactly
                                       the streaming path). Post-fix: (A) pinned follows growth, dist stays
                                       0; (B) down-wheel tick at bottom no longer breaks following (pre-fix
                                       repro froze permanently); (C) scrolled-up reader is not yanked while
                                       chunks stream, and the scroll-to-bottom button appears; (D) returning
                                       near bottom + down-wheel re-pins and following resumes. Button
                                       behavior unchanged.
                                       - Two verification caveats: the dev app is shared (other agents'
                                       messages remounted the list mid-test a few times, so tests were
                                       repeated on clean state), and note that when the Chrome window is
                                       occluded, macOS pauses rendering — ResizeObserver/rAF don't deliver,
                                       so auto-follow legitimately stalls until the window is visible again
                                       (matches the "hidden tabs throttle rendering" memory; not a bug in
                                       this component).

                                       Not committed, per instructions.</result>
                                       <usage><subagent_tokens>111299</subagent_tokens><tool_uses>68</tool_u
                                       ses><duration_ms>1226938</duration_ms></usage>
                                       </task-notification>

                                       following-bottom mode — but every wheel/touchmove flips to
                                       free-scrolling,
                                       and the only way back is a scroll event within 8px of the bottom. A
                                       downward or horizontal wheel tick while already AT the bottom moves
                                       nothing, so no scroll event fires and the pin is silently lost
                                       (constant
                                       with macOS trackpad inertia). Wrapper-level onWheel in
                                       message-scroller:
                                       down-wheel within 100px of the bottom re-pins via scrollToEnd,
                                       deltaY=0 at
                                       the bottom restores the pin (horizontal pans no longer unpin),
                                       scrolling
                                       up stays unpinned — readers are never yanked. Live-verified all four
                                       cases against simulated streaming.

                                       Co-Authored-By: Claude Fable 5 <noreply@anthropic.com>" --
                                       client/src/components/ui/message-scroller.tsx && echo COMMITTED
                                       why: Commit chat bottom-anchoring fix

                                       <task-id>a61850497c4635a43</task-id>
                                       <tool-use-id>toolu_01PSTUTCPX553r38ZjNNjCgQ</tool-use-id>

                                       <status>completed</status>
                                       <summary>Agent "Screenshot-per-voice-turn revisit" finished</summary>
                                       <note>A task-notification fires each time this agent stops with no
                                       live background children of its own. The user can send it another
                                       message and resume it, so the same task-id may notify more than
                                       once.</note>
                                       <result>The investigation is complete. No code change is warranted —
                                       here is the analysis.

                                       ## 1. Ordering feasibility: poor

                                       The session is configured server-side at mint time
                                       (`/Users/steve/projects/explore/server/src/voice.ts:96-106`) with
                                       `turn_detection: { type: "semantic_vad" }` and the default
                                       `create_response: true` — the server auto-fires response creation the
                                       moment the audio buffer commits. The client
                                       (`/Users/steve/projects/explore/client/src/hooks/use-voice.ts`) never
                                       sends `session.update` and has no hook to delay the response.

                                       To attach an image to the *current* user turn, a
                                       `conversation.item.create` with `input_image` must land before that
                                       auto-response. The only client trigger available is
                                       `input_audio_buffer.speech_started` (use-voice.ts:488), so capture +
                                       shrink + send must beat utterance-end plus the VAD commit. That is a
                                       race the client often loses: `captureMainView` uses html-to-image's
                                       full-DOM clone
                                       (`/Users/steve/projects/explore/client/src/lib/capture.ts`) —
                                       hundreds of ms to seconds of main-thread work — while the deictic
                                       utterances that motivate the feature ("make this shorter") are
                                       exactly the short ones that commit fastest. A lost race means the
                                       image lands *after* `response.created` and silently attaches to the
                                       next turn, doubly stale.

                                       The "attach when the transcript contains a deictic marker" variant is
                                       dead on arrival:
                                       `conversation.item.input_audio_transcription.completed`
                                       (use-voice.ts:510) is an async side-channel that typically arrives
                                       after response generation is already underway. You learn the turn was
                                       deictic only after the response it should have informed. The clean
                                       fix (`create_response: false` + client-side `response.create` after
                                       the image) is a server config change outside the allowed scope and
                                       adds capture latency to every turn.

                                       ## 2. Cost: 30–100x worse, and it destroys the context window

                                       A ≤1024px JPEG (`SNAPSHOT_MAX_EDGE = 1024`, use-voice.ts:104) is
                                       roughly 600–800 vision tokens under the tile-based formula (~85 base
                                       + ~170 per 512px tile → ~765 for 1024×1024). Per image that is
                                       pennies. The problem is that Realtime conversations carry every prior
                                       item into every subsequent response:

                                       - 30 turns × ~765 tokens ≈ 23K tokens of resident images — which by
                                       itself nearly fills the Realtime model's ~32K context, forcing
                                       truncation of the actual dialogue and instructions.
                                       - Cumulative rebilling ≈ 765 × Σ(1..30) ≈ 355K image-input tokens ≈
                                       order of $1–2 per chatty session (caching softens but does not remove
                                       this), versus the on-demand tool's typical 0–3 screenshots ≈
                                       $0.01–0.05.

                                       ## 3. UX: on-demand is fresher, not staler

                                       - **Staleness inverts the intuition**: a speech-start capture shows
                                       the screen *before* the user finished the request and before the
                                       previous turn's tool effects settled. `take_screenshot` captures at
                                       call time — maximally fresh. The "cheap capture-on-speech-start, send
                                       when take_screenshot is called" variant is strictly worse: same
                                       per-utterance jank, staler image than today's call-time capture.
                                       - **Jank**: toCanvas DOM cloning on every `speech_started` is a
                                       visible main-thread stutter exactly when the user starts talking;
                                       semantic VAD also fires `speech_started` on false
                                       positives/background noise, so idle rooms burn captures.
                                       - **Deixis mostly resolves structurally**: `get_app_state` already
                                       carries selection/scroll/visible-doc, which answers "this" for most
                                       edits without pixels.

                                       ## What I did

                                       Nothing implemented — the analysis clearly favors the status quo on
                                       all three axes (ordering unreliable with server-VAD auto-response,
                                       cost/context blowup, worse freshness). No files were modified, so no
                                       typecheck/build was run.

                                       **Recommendation**: close the blitz row as "keep on-demand
                                       take_screenshot + get_app_state deixis guidance." If deixis quality
                                       ever proves insufficient in practice, the right lever is server-side
                                       (`create_response: false` with client-orchestrated response creation
                                       in `server/src/voice.ts`), not per-turn attachment from the
                                       client.</result>
                                       <usage><subagent_tokens>33821</subagent_tokens><tool_uses>7</tool_use
                                       s><duration_ms>101993</duration_ms></usage>
                                       </task-notification>

                                       ## renameDoc contract as landed

                                       `renameDoc(wikiDir, from, to)` — both paths wiki-relative and
                                       `wikiDocPath`-validated at every surface (voice `requireWikiPath`,
                                       MCP `requirePath`, both arguments):

                                       - **Same extension required** (case-insensitive): a rename never
                                       rewrites content, so cross-type renames (`.md`→`.oui`) are refused
                                       with a teaching error saying to create a new file instead. Decision
                                       encoded in the doc comment.
                                       - **No overwrite, atomically**: implemented as `link(2)` +
                                       `unlink(2)` — plain `rename(2)` silently replaces targets, but `link`
                                       fails with `EEXIST`. Both names briefly coexist; the source never
                                       vanishes before the target exists. `EEXIST` → "already exists —
                                       refusing to overwrite"; `ENOENT` → missing-source teaching error;
                                       same-path no-op refused explicitly.
                                       - **Parent dirs of the target created**, like `createDoc`. Works for
                                       any extension including `.oui`.
                                       - Voice returns `{renamed, to, url}`; MCP returns "Renamed X to Y
                                       (now served at /docs/Y)."

                                       ## Empty-content decision

                                       **Reject everywhere, boundary in the service**: `createDoc` throws
                                       `refusing to create "X" with empty content` — an empty create is a
                                       mistaken call, and a lone-newline file renders as a puzzling blank
                                       page. Both tool schemas mirror it with `min(1)` (voice already had
                                       it; MCP gained it). Also: the exists-check race is gone (`writeFile`
                                       flag `"wx"`, `EEXIST` mapped to the refuse-overwrite error), and that
                                       error is now surface-neutral ("edit the existing file instead of
                                       creating it again" — no tool names).

                                       ## Watcher verification

                                       Verified empirically (probe script driving `fs.watch(recursive)`
                                       exactly as `index.ts` sets it up): link+unlink fires `rename` events
                                       for **both** the old and new paths, so `wiki:changed` broadcasts for
                                       `/docs/&lt;old&gt;` and `/docs/&lt;new&gt;`. A client viewing the old
                                       path gets its change signal; no protocol work needed.

                                       ## Prompt line for server/prompts/wiki.md (not touched — add later)

                                       &gt; `rename_file` renames or moves a wiki file to a new path (the
                                       extension must stay the same, and the target must not already exist).

                                       ## Validation points
                                       A new module-private `ouiProblem(content)` in wiki-service.ts parses
                                       with `createParser(uiLibrary.toJSONSchema())` — the same lang-core
                                       parser and the server's schema mirror of the client renderer's
                                       library (client uses `Renderer` from `@openuidev/react-lang` over the
                                       same components). It flags, in order: zero statements parsed (the
                                       hallucinated-indentation case — the parser reports no error for
                                       prose, just `statementCount: 0`), any prop-validation error (unknown
                                       component / missing required prop — the parser redacts those nodes),
                                       truncated input (`meta.incomplete`), and `root === null` (renders
                                       empty). The parser is built lazily once.

                                       - **createDoc** (path ends `.oui`): refuses before write, file never
                                       exists. Error text: `refusing to create "&lt;rel&gt;" — not valid
                                       OpenUI Lang (&lt;reason&gt;); artifacts are OpenUI Lang \`name =
                                       Component(...)\` statements and need a root component`
                                       - **editDoc** (the str_replace path, voice `edit_doc`): applies the
                                       replacement in memory, validates the **result**, refuses before
                                       `writeFile` so the file is bit-for-bit unchanged. Error text:
                                       `refusing this edit — "&lt;rel&gt;" would no longer be valid OpenUI
                                       Lang (&lt;reason&gt;); artifacts are OpenUI Lang \`name =
                                       Component(...)\` statements and need a root component. The file is
                                       unchanged.`

                                       Both are surface-neutral (no tool names), matching the createDoc
                                       duplicate-path convention; `&lt;reason&gt;` carries the parser's
                                       message plus the offending statement name when known (e.g. `Unknown
                                       component "Stak" — not found in catalog or builtins (in statement
                                       "main")`).
